<p>In 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Bonneville_Power_Administration" title="Bonneville Power Administration">Bonneville Power Administration</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_United_States" title="Northwestern United States">Northwestern United States</a> created an experimental program to absorb excess wind and hydro power generated at night or during stormy periods that are accompanied by high winds. Under central control, home appliances absorb surplus energy by heating ceramic bricks in <a href="/wiki/Storage_heater" title="Storage heater">special space heaters</a> to hundreds of degrees and by boosting the temperature of modified <a href="/wiki/Storage_water_heater" title="Storage water heater">hot water heater tanks</a>. After charging, the appliances provide home heating and hot water as needed. The experimental system was created as a result of a severe 2010 storm that overproduced renewable energy to the extent that all conventional power sources were shut down, or in the case of a nuclear power plant, reduced to its lowest possible operating level, leaving a large area running almost completely on renewable energy.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-2011.11.05_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-2011.11.05-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-2010.07.07_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-2010.07.07-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another advanced method used at the former <a href="/wiki/The_Solar_Project" title="The Solar Project">Solar Two project</a> in the United States and the <a href="/wiki/Gemasolar_Thermosolar_Plant" title="Gemasolar Thermosolar Plant">Solar Tres Power Tower</a> in Spain uses <a href="/wiki/Thermal_energy_storage#Molten_salt_technology" title="Thermal energy storage">molten salt</a> to store thermal energy captured from the sun and then convert it and dispatch it as electrical power. The system pumps molten salt through a tower or other special conduits to be heated by the sun. Insulated tanks store the solution. Electricity is produced by turning water to steam that is fed to <a href="/wiki/Turbine" title="Turbine">turbines</a>.</p>
<p>Since the early 21st century batteries have been applied to utility scale load-leveling and <a href="/wiki/Utility_frequency" title="Utility frequency">frequency regulation</a> capabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-2010.07.28_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-2010.07.28-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Vehicle-to-grid" title="Vehicle-to-grid">vehicle-to-grid</a> storage, electric vehicles that are plugged into the energy grid can deliver stored electrical energy from their batteries into the grid when needed.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Generation">Generation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Energy_storage&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Generation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Chemical fuels remain the dominant form of energy storage for electricity generation. Natural gas is crowding out other forms, such as oil and coal.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_conditioning">Air conditioning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Energy_storage&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Air conditioning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ice_storage_air_conditioning" title="Ice storage air conditioning">Ice storage air conditioning</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Thermal_energy_storage" title="Thermal energy storage">Thermal energy storage</a> (TES) can be used for <a href="/wiki/Air_conditioning" title="Air conditioning">air conditioning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Calmac_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calmac-75">[75]</a></sup> It is most widely used for cooling single large buildings and/or groups of smaller buildings. Commercial air conditioning systems are the biggest contributors to peak electrical loads. In 2009, thermal storage was used in over 3,300 buildings in over 35 countries. It works by creating ice at night and using the ice to for cooling during the hotter daytime periods.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-2014.04.21_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-2014.04.21-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>The most popular technique is <a href="/wiki/Thermal_energy_storage#Air_conditioning" title="Thermal energy storage">ice storage</a>, which requires less space than water and is less costly than fuel cells or flywheels. In this application, a standard chiller runs at night to produce an ice pile. Water then circulates through the pile during the day to chill water that would normally be the chiller's daytime output.</p>
<p>A partial storage system minimizes capital investment by running the chillers nearly 24 hours a day. At night, they produce ice for storage and during the day they chill water. Water circulating through the melting ice augments the production of chilled water. Such a system makes ice for 16 to 18 hours a day and melts ice for six hours a day. Capital expenditures are reduced because the chillers can be just 40 - 50% of the size needed for a conventional, no-storage design. Storage sufficient to store half a day's available heat is usually adequate.</p>
<p>A full storage system shuts off the chillers during peak load hours. Capital costs are higher, as such a system requires larger chillers and a larger ice storage system.</p>
<p>This ice is produced when electrical utility rates are lower.<sup id="cite_ref-DistributedEnergy.com_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DistributedEnergy.com-76">[76]</a></sup> Off-peak cooling systems can lower energy costs. The U.S. <a href="/wiki/Green_Building_Council" title="Green Building Council">Green Building Council</a> has developed the <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design</a> (LEED) program to encourage the design of reduced-environmental impact buildings. Off-peak cooling may help toward LEED Certification.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Thermal storage for heating is less common than for cooling. An example of thermal storage is storing solar heat to be used for heating at night.</p>
<p>Latent heat can also be stored in technical <a href="/wiki/Phase-change_material" title="Phase-change material">phase change materials</a> (PCMs). These can be encapsulated in wall and ceiling panels, to moderate room temperatures.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Energy_storage&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Liquid <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon_fuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrocarbon fuel">hydrocarbon fuels</a> are the most commonly used forms of energy storage for use in <a href="/wiki/Transportation" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation">transportation</a>. Other energy carriers such as <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a> can be used to avoid producing greenhouse gases.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electronics">Electronics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Energy_storage&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Electronics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Capacitors are widely used in <a href="/wiki/Electronic_circuit" title="Electronic circuit">electronic circuits</a> for blocking <a href="/wiki/Direct_current" title="Direct current">direct current</a> while allowing <a href="/wiki/Alternating_current" title="Alternating current">alternating current</a> to pass. In <a href="/wiki/Analog_filter" class="mw-redirect" title="Analog filter">analog filter</a> networks, they smooth the output of <a href="/wiki/Power_supply" title="Power supply">power supplies</a>. In <a href="/wiki/LC_circuit" title="LC circuit">resonant circuits</a> they tune <a href="/wiki/Radio" title="Radio">radios</a> to particular <a href="/wiki/Frequency" title="Frequency">frequencies</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_transmission" title="Electric power transmission">electric power transmission</a> systems they stabilize voltage and power flow.<sup id="cite_ref-Bird_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bird-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_cases">Use cases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Energy_storage&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Use cases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy_International_Energy_Storage_Database" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Department of Energy International Energy Storage Database">United States Department of Energy International Energy Storage Database</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy_International_Energy_Storage_Database" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Department of Energy International Energy Storage Database">United States Department of Energy International Energy Storage Database</a> (IESDB), is a free-access database of energy storage projects and policies funded by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">United States Department of Energy</a> Office of Electricity and <a href="/wiki/Sandia_National_Labs" class="mw-redirect" title="Sandia National Labs">Sandia National Labs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DOE_Global_Energy_Storage_Database_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DOE_Global_Energy_Storage_Database-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storage_capacity">Storage capacity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Energy_storage&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Storage capacity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Storage capacity</b> is the amount of energy extracted from a <a href="/wiki/Power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Power plant">power plant</a> energy storage system; usually measured in <a href="/wiki/Joule" title="Joule">joules</a> or <a href="/wiki/Kilowatt_hour" title="Kilowatt hour">kilowatt-hours</a> and their multiples, it may be given in number of hours of electricity production at power plant <a href="/wiki/Nameplate_capacity" title="Nameplate capacity">nameplate capacity</a>; when storage is of primary type (i.e., thermal or pumped-water), output is sourced only with the power plant embedded storage system.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Energy_storage&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The economics of Energy Storage strictly depends on the reserve service requested, and several uncertainty factors affect the profitability of Energy Storage. Therefore, not every Energy Storage is technically and economically suitable for the storage of several MWh, and the optimal size of the Energy Storage is market and location dependent.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Moreover, ESS are affected by several risks, e.g.:<sup id="cite_ref-Locatelli_114.E2.80.93131_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Locatelli_114.E2.80.93131-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>1) techno-economic risks, which are related to the specific technology;</p>
<p>2) Market risks, which are the factors that affect the electricity supply system;</p>
<p>3) Regulation and policy risks.</p>
<p>Therefore, traditional techniques based on deterministic <a href="/wiki/Discounted_cash_flow" title="Discounted cash flow">Discounted Cash Flow</a> (DCF) for the investment appraisal are not fully adequate to evaluate these risks and uncertainties and the investor’s flexibility to deal with them. Hence, the literature recommends to assess the value of risks and uncertainties through the Real Option Analysis (ROA), which is a valuable method in uncertain contexts.<sup id="cite_ref-Locatelli_114.E2.80.93131_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Locatelli_114.E2.80.93131-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>The economic valuation of large-scale applications (including pumped hydro storage and compressed air) considers benefits including: wind curtailment avoidance, grid congestion avoidance, price arbitrage and carbon free energy delivery.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-2014.04.21_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-2014.04.21-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Loisel_et_al_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Loisel_et_al-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-2012.01.03_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-2012.01.03-85">[85]</a></sup> In one technical assessment by the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon Electricity Industry Centre</a>, economic goals could be met with batteries if energy storage were achievable at a capital cost of $30 to $50 per kilowatt-hour of storage capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-2014.04.21_70-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-2014.04.21-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>A metric for calculating the energy efficiency of storage systems is Energy Storage On Energy Invested (ESOI) which is the useful energy used to make the storage system divided into the lifetime energy storage. For lithium ion batteries this is around 10, and for lead acid batteries it is about 2. Other forms of storage such as pumped hydroelectric storage generally have higher ESOI, such as 210.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Energy_storage&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Energy_storage&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The German Federal government has allocated €200M (approximately US$270M) for advanced research, as well as providing a further €50M to subsidize battery storage for use with residential rooftop solar panels, according to a representative of the German Energy Storage Association.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes-2013.10.13_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-2013.10.13-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens AG</a> commissioned a production-research plant to open in 2015 at the <i>Zentrum für Sonnenenergie und Wasserstoff (ZSW,</i> the German Center for Solar Energy and Hydrogen Research in the <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">State of Baden-Württemberg</a>), a university/industry collaboration in Stuttgart, Ulm and Widderstall, staffed by approximately 350 scientists, researchers, engineers, and technicians. The plant develops new near-production manufacturing materials and processes (NPMM&amp;P) using a computerized <a href="/wiki/SCADA" title="SCADA">Supervisory Control and Data Acquisition</a> (SCADA) system. Its goals will enable the expansion of <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery" title="Rechargeable battery">rechargeable battery</a> production with both increased quality and reduced manufacturing costs.<sup id="cite_ref-Physics.org.a_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Physics.org.a-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ZSW-BW.de_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZSW-BW.de-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Energy_storage&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2014, research and test centers opened to evaluate energy storage technologies. Among them was the Advanced Systems Test Laboratory at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison" title="University of Wisconsin–Madison">University of Wisconsin at Madison</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">Wisconsin State</a>, which partnered with battery manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Controls" title="Johnson Controls">Johnson Controls</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Milwaukee_Journal_Sentinel-2014.05.05_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Milwaukee_Journal_Sentinel-2014.05.05-90">[90]</a></sup> The laboratory was created as part of the university's newly opened <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Energy_Institute" title="Wisconsin Energy Institute">Wisconsin Energy Institute</a>. Their goals include the evaluation of state-of-the-art and next generation <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_battery" title="Electric vehicle battery">electric vehicle batteries</a>, including their use as grid supplements.<sup id="cite_ref-Milwaukee_Journal_Sentinel-2014.05.05_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Milwaukee_Journal_Sentinel-2014.05.05-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" class="mw-redirect" title="New York (state)">State of New York</a> unveiled its New York Battery and Energy Storage Technology (NY-BEST) Test and Commercialization Center at <a href="/wiki/Eastman_Business_Park" title="Eastman Business Park">Eastman Business Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_New_York" title="Rochester, New York">Rochester, New York</a>, at a cost of $23&#160;million for its almost 1,700&#160;m<sup>2</sup> laboratory. The center includes the Center for Future Energy Systems, a collaboration between <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ithaca,_New_York" title="Ithaca, New York">Ithaca, New York</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</a> in <a href="/wiki/Troy,_New_York" title="Troy, New York">Troy, New York</a>. NY-BEST tests, validates and independently certifies diverse forms of energy storage intended for commercial use.<sup id="cite_ref-Democrat_and_Chronicle-2014.04.30_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Democrat_and_Chronicle-2014.04.30-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Energy_storage&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the United Kingdom, some fourteen industry and government agencies allied with seven British universities in May 2014 to create the <a href="/wiki/SUPERGEN_Energy_Storage_Hub" class="mw-redirect" title="SUPERGEN Energy Storage Hub">SUPERGEN Energy Storage Hub</a> in order to assist in the coordination of energy storage technology research and development.<sup id="cite_ref-HVNPlus_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HVNPlus-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ECNMag.com-2014.05.02_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECNMag.com-2014.05.02-93">[93]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Energy_storage&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>General</b></p>
<ul>
<li>Barringer, Felicity. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://green.blogs.nytimes.com/2010/10/01/in-california-a-grid-storage-mandate/">Green Blog: In California, a Grid Storage Mandate</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, October 1, 2010.</li>
<li>Baxter, Richard. Energy Storage: A Nontechnical Guide, September 10, 2005. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/159370027X" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1-59370-027-X</a></li>
<li>Belli, Brita. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://wheels.blogs.nytimes.com/2013/04/08/battery-university-aims-to-train-a-workforce-for-next-generation-energy-storage/">‘Battery University’ Aims to Train a Work Force for Next-Generation Energy Storage</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, April 8, 2013. Discusses a professional development program at <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_State_University" title="San Jose State University">San Jose State University</a>.</li>
<li>Browne, Malcome W. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/1988/01/06/business/business-technology-advances-new-hunt-for-ideal-energy-storage-system.html">New Hunt for Ideal Energy Storage System</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, January 6, 1988. Discusses <a href="/wiki/Superconducting_magnetic_energy_storage" title="Superconducting magnetic energy storage">superconducting magnetic energy storage</a>.</li>
<li>Cardwell, Diane. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2013/07/17/business/energy-environment/battery-seen-as-way-to-cut-heat-related-power-losses.html">Battery Seen as Way to Cut Heat-Related Power Losses</a>, July 16, 2013 online and July 17, 2013 in print on July 17, 2013, on page B1 in the New York City edition of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, p. B1. Discusses Eos Energy Systems' <a href="/wiki/Zinc%E2%80%93air_battery#Grid_storage" title="Zinc–air battery">Zinc–air batteries</a>.</li>
<li>Cardwell, Diane. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2013/12/05/business/energy-environment/solarcity-to-use-batteries-from-tesla-for-energy-storage.html">SolarCity to Use Batteries From Tesla for Energy Storage</a>, December 4, 2013 on line, and December 5, 2013 in the New York City edition of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, p. B-2. Discusses <a href="/wiki/SolarCity" title="SolarCity">SolarCity</a>, DemandLogic and <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors" class="mw-redirect" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla Motors</a>.</li>
<li>Galbraith, Kate. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2010/11/07/us/07ttbattery.html?pagewanted=all">In Presidio, a Grasp at the Holy Grail of Energy Storage</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, November 6, 2010.</li>
<li>Galbraith, Kate. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2013/10/03/business/energy-environment/Filling-the-Gaps-in-the-Flow-of-Renewable-Energy.html">Filling the Gaps in the Flow of Renewable Energy</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, October 22, 2013.</li>
<li>Gies, Erica. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2010/09/30/business/energy-environment/30iht-renstore.html?pagewanted=all">The Challenge of Storing Energy on a Large Scale</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, September 29, 2010.</li>
<li>Gies, Erica. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2010/11/29/business/energy-environment/29iht-rbogferc.html?pagewanted=all&amp;_r=0&amp;gwh=402884C2E19C695EA255CCF207D8BB22">Making the Consumer an Active Participant in the Grid</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, November 29, 2010. Discusses <a href="/wiki/Distributed_generation" title="Distributed generation">distributed generation</a> and the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Energy_Regulatory_Commission" title="Federal Energy Regulatory Commission">Federal Energy Regulatory Commission</a>.</li>
<li>Gies, Erica. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2012/10/02/business/energy-environment/a-storage-solution-is-in-the-air.html?pagewanted=all">I.H.T. Special Report: Global Clean Energy: A Storage Solution Is in the Air</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_International_New_York_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="The International New York Times">The International Herald Tribune</a></i>, October 1, 2012. Retrieved from NYTimes.com website. Discusses SustainX, LightSail Energy, and both <a href="/wiki/Compressed_air_energy_storage#Adiabatic_.28isentropic.29_storage" title="Compressed air energy storage">adiabatic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Compressed_air_energy_storage#Isothermal_storage" title="Compressed air energy storage">isothermal compressed air energy storage</a>.</li>
<li>Huggins, Robert. Energy storage. Springer Science &amp; Business Media, 2010.</li>
<li>Kumagai, Jean. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://spectrum.ieee.org/energywise/energy/renewables/underwater-energy-bags-for-the-london-array">How Much Energy Storage Do You Need to Back Up the London Array?</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/IEEE_Spectrum" title="IEEE Spectrum">IEEE Spectrum</a></i>, July 15, 2014.</li>
<li>LaMonica, Martin. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.smithsonianmag.com/innovation/big-bet-how-store-energy-cheaply-180951829">A Big Bet on How to Store Energy, Cheaply</a>, June 24, 2014, <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_(magazine)" title="Smithsonian (magazine)"><i>Smithsonian</i> magazine</a> website. Retrieved from Smithsonian.com July 20, 2014. Discusses CAES, SustainX, LightSail Energy, and others.</li>
<li>Malewitz, Jim. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2014/06/22/us/project-tests-new-storage-for-energy.html">Project Tests New Storage for Energy</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> website, June 21, 2014, and in print on June 22, 2014, on p. A27A of the National edition.</li>
<li>Middlesboro Daily News. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=spxBAAAAIBAJ&amp;sjid=eakMAAAAIBAJ&amp;pg=6415,708510">The Case For A Fifth Wheel</a>, Middlesboro, Kentucky: Middlesboro Daily News, January 15, 1974, p.&#160;4. Discusses research into flywheel powered autos.</li>
<li>Ricketts, Camille. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/external/venturebeat/2010/08/10/10venturebeat-doe-charges-up-flywheels-finalizes-43m-loan-54486.html">DOE Charges Up Flywheels, Finalizes $43M Loan to Beacon Power</a>, VentureBeat, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, August 10, 2010. Discusses <a href="/wiki/Beacon_Power" title="Beacon Power">Beacon Power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flywheel_energy_storage" title="Flywheel energy storage">flywheel energy storage</a>.</li>
<li>Sorkin, Andrew Ross. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://dealbook.nytimes.com/2010/09/30/storage-clean-energys-killer-app/">Storage: Clean Energy’s Killer App</a>, DealBook, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, September 30, 2010.</li>
<li>Sorkin, Andrew Ross. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://dealbook.nytimes.com/2012/11/29/despite-setbacks-investor-is-bullish-on-clean-technology/">Despite Setbacks, Investor Is Bullish on Clean Technology</a>, DealBook, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, November 29, 2012. Discusses LightSail and Khosla Ventures.</li>
<li>Wald, Matthew L. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://green.blogs.nytimes.com/2009/12/28/harnessing-the-sun-to-store-the-wind/?gwh=F424D5236895F26B2B4347B060FACBAD">Green Blog: Harnessing the Sun to Store the Wind</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, December 28, 2009. <li>Wald, Matthew L. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://green.blogs.nytimes.com/2010/01/27/storing-energy-as-ice/?gwh=ABAA16FD8571356FA9FC946D3D2AD3F7">Green Blog: Storing Energy as Ice?</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, January 27, 2010. <li>Wald, Matthew L. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://green.blogs.nytimes.com/2011/04/14/arpa-e-is-poised-to-put-products-on-the-grid/">Green Blog: ARPA-E Is Poised to Put Products on the Grid</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, April 14, 2011. Discusses: <a href="/wiki/ARPA-E" title="ARPA-E">Advanced Research Projects Agency</a> (ARPA-E), General Compression, <a href="/wiki/CAES" class="mw-redirect" title="CAES">CAES</a>.</li>
<li>Wald, Matthew L. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://green.blogs.nytimes.com/2011/05/18/can-batteries-replace-power-generators/">Can Batteries Replace Power Generators?</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, May 18, 2011. Discusses: AES Energy Storage, Long Island Power Authority.</li>
<li>Wald, Matthew L. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2011/10/29/science/earth/batteries-on-a-wind-farm-help-control-power-output.html?scp=1&amp;sq=elkins%20batteries%20wald&amp;st=cse">Batteries at a Wind Farm Help Control Output</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, October 28, 2011. Discusses: <a href="/wiki/AES_Corporation" title="AES Corporation">AES Corporation</a>, energy storage at wind farms.</li>
<li>Wald, Matthew L. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2012/01/03/business/energy-environment/building-storehouses-for-the-suns-energy-for-use-after-dark.html?pagewanted=all">Storehouses for Solar Energy Can Step In When the Sun Goes Down</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, January 2, 2012. Discusses <a href="/wiki/Thermal_energy_storage#Molten_salt_technology" title="Thermal energy storage">molten salt thermal storage</a>, <a href="/wiki/SolarReserve" title="SolarReserve">SolarReserve</a>, Brightsource, <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_tower" title="Solar power tower">solar power towers</a>.</li>
<li>Wald, Matthew L. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://green.blogs.nytimes.com/2012/02/08/surplus-renewable-energy-an-update/">Green Blog: Surplus Renewable Energy: An Update</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, February 8, 2012.</li>
<li>Wald, Matthew L. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://green.blogs.nytimes.com/2012/05/09/is-that-onions-you-smell-or-battery-juice/#more-140249">Green Blog: Is That Onions You Smell? <li>Wald, Matthew L. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2013/10/18/business/energy-environment/arizona-utility-tries-storing-solar-energy-for-use-in-the-dark.html?_r=0">Arizona Utility Tries Storing Solar Energy for Use in the Dark</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, October 18, 2013, p. Discusses <a href="/wiki/BrightSource_Energy" title="BrightSource Energy">BrightSource Energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_Power_Research_Institute" title="Electric Power Research Institute">Electric Power Research Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivanpah_Solar_Power_Facility" title="Ivanpah Solar Power Facility">Ivanpah Solar Power Facility project</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Solana_Generating_Station" title="Solana Generating Station">Solana Generating Station project</a>.</li>
<li>Wald, Matthew L. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2013/12/24/business/energy-environment/catching-some-rays-in-california-and-storing-them.html">Catching Rays in California, and Storing Them</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, December 23, 2013 online, and in print on December 24, 2013, p. B3 of the New York edition. Discusses the <a href="/wiki/California_Public_Utilities_Commission" title="California Public Utilities Commission">California Public Utilities Commission</a>'s role in mandating the use of energy storage within that state.</li>
<li>Wald, Matthew L. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2014/01/09/business/energy-environment/from-harvard-a-cheaper-storage-battery.html">From Harvard, a Cheaper Storage Battery</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, January 8, 2014. F4. Published online March 30, 2011. Discusses <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery" title="Rechargeable battery">batteries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lithium_ion_battery" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithium ion battery">lithium ion battery</a>.</li>
<li>Witkin, Jim. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://green.blogs.nytimes.com/2011/04/27/a-second-life-for-the-electric-car-battery/">Green Blog: A Second Life for the Electric Car Battery</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, April 27, 2011. Describes: ABB; Community Energy Storage for the use of electric vehicle batteries for grid energy storage.</li>
